   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">International Workers' Day</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about International Workers Day on 1 May, a holiday sometimes called May Day. See <a href="/wiki/May_Day" title="May Day">May Day</a> for the traditional spring holiday. See <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a> for other labour-related holidays.
      </div> 
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Celebration in the international labour movement on May Day
      </div>

      <p><b>International Workers' Day</b>, also known as <b>Labour Day</b> in most countries<sup id="cite_ref-GMGApr2008_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMGApr2008-1">[1]</a></sup> and often referred to as <b>May Day</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> is a celebration of <a href="/wiki/Wage_labour" title="Wage labour">labourers</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">working classes</a> that is promoted by the international <a href="/wiki/Labour_movement" title="Labour movement">labour movement</a> and occurs every year on <a href="/wiki/May_Day" title="May Day">May Day</a> (1 May).<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Foner_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foner-5">[5]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>While it may belong to a tradition of spring festivals, the date was chosen in 1889 for political reasons by the <a href="/wiki/International_Workers_Congresses_of_Paris,_1889" title="International Workers Congresses of Paris, 1889">Marxist International Socialist Congress</a>, which met in Paris and established the <a href="/wiki/Second_International" title="Second International">Second International</a> as a successor to the earlier <a href="/wiki/International_Workingmen%27s_Association" title="International Workingmen's Association">International Workingmen's Association</a>. They adopted a resolution for a "great international demonstration" in support of working-class demands for the eight-hour day. The date had been chosen by the <a href="/wiki/American_Federation_of_Labor" title="American Federation of Labor">American Federation of Labor</a> to continue an earlier campaign for the eight-hour day in the United States, which had culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Haymarket_affair" title="Haymarket affair">Haymarket affair</a>, which occurred in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> on 4 May 1886. May Day subsequently became an annual event.<sup id="cite_ref-Foner_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foner-5">[5]</a></sup> The 1904 <a href="/wiki/International_Socialist_Congress,_Amsterdam_1904" title="International Socialist Congress, Amsterdam 1904">Sixth Conference of the Second International</a>, called on "all Social Democratic Party organisations and trade unions of all countries to demonstrate energetically on the First of May for the legal establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Eight-hour_day" title="Eight-hour day">eight-hour day</a>, for the class demands of the <a href="/wiki/Proletariat" title="Proletariat">proletariat</a>, and for <a href="/wiki/World_peace" title="World peace">universal peace</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-Lunacharsky_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lunacharsky-6">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first of May is a national, <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">public holiday</a> in many countries across the world, in most cases as "International Workers' Day" or a similar name. Some countries celebrate a <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a> on other dates significant to them, such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, which celebrate <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">Labor Day</a> on the first Monday of September. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin">Origin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>On 21 April 1856, Australian <a href="/wiki/Stonemasons" class="mw-redirect" title="Stonemasons">stonemasons</a> in <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a> undertook a mass stoppage as part of the <a href="/wiki/Eight-hour_day" title="Eight-hour day">eight-hour workday</a> movement.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> It became a yearly commemoration, inspiring American workers to have their first stoppage.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> 1 May was chosen to be International Workers' Day to commemorate the 1886 <a href="/wiki/Haymarket_affair" title="Haymarket affair">Haymarket affair</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> In that year beginning on 1 May, there was a general strike for the eight-hour workday. On 4 May, the police acted to disperse a public assembly in support of the strike when an unidentified person threw a bomb. The police responded by firing on the workers. The event led to the deaths of seven police officers and at least thirty-eight civilians; sixty police officers were injured, as were one hundred and fifteen civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Hundreds of labour leaders and sympathizers were later rounded-up and four were executed by hanging, after a trial that was seen as a miscarriage of justice.<sup id="cite_ref-the_bomb_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the_bomb-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[nb 1]</a></sup> The following day on 5 May, in <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee" title="Milwaukee">Milwaukee, Wisconsin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_National_Guard" title="Wisconsin National Guard">state militia</a> fired on a crowd of strikers killing seven, including a schoolboy and a man feeding chickens in his yard.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-15">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1889, a meeting in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> was held by the <a href="/wiki/International_Workers_Congresses_of_Paris,_1889" title="International Workers Congresses of Paris, 1889">first congress</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Second_International" title="Second International">Second International</a>, following a proposal by <a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raymond_Lavigne_(syndicaliste)" class="extiw" title="fr:Raymond Lavigne (syndicaliste)">Raymond Lavigne</a> that called for international demonstrations on the 1890 anniversary of the Chicago protests.<sup id="cite_ref-Foner_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foner-5">[5]</a></sup> On May 1, 1890, the call encouraged May Day demonstrations took place in the United States and most countries in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-andy_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-andy-16">[15]</a></sup> Demonstrations were also held in Chile and Peru.<sup id="cite_ref-andy_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-andy-16">[15]</a></sup> May Day was formally recognized as an annual event at the International's <a href="/wiki/International_Socialist_Labor_Congress_of_Brussels,_1891" title="International Socialist Labor Congress of Brussels, 1891">second congress</a> in 1891.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> Subsequently, the <a href="/wiki/May_Day_riots_of_1894" title="May Day riots of 1894">May Day riots of 1894</a> occurred. The <a href="/wiki/International_Socialist_Congress,_Amsterdam_1904" title="International Socialist Congress, Amsterdam 1904">International Socialist Congress, Amsterdam 1904</a> called on "all <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">Social Democratic</a> Party organisations and <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade unions</a> of all countries to demonstrate energetically on the First of May for the legal establishment of the 8-hour day, for the class demands of the proletariat, and for universal peace."<sup id="cite_ref-Lunacharsky_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lunacharsky-6">[6]</a></sup> The congress made it "mandatory upon the <a href="/wiki/Proletarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Proletarian">proletarian</a> organisations of all countries to stop work on 1 May, wherever it is possible without injury to the workers."<sup id="cite_ref-Lunacharsky_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lunacharsky-6">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the United States and Canada, a September holiday, called Labor or <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a>, was first proposed in the 1880s. In 1882, <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Maguire_(labor_activist)" title="Matthew Maguire (labor activist)">Matthew Maguire</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Machinist" title="Machinist">machinist</a>, first proposed a Labor Day holiday on the first Monday of September<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[nb 2]</a></sup> while serving as secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Labor_Union" title="Central Labor Union">Central Labor Union</a> (CLU) of New York.<sup id="cite_ref-labordept_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-labordept-19">[18]</a></sup> Others argue that it was first proposed by <a href="/wiki/Peter_J._McGuire" title="Peter J. McGuire">Peter J. McGuire</a> of the <a href="/wiki/American_Federation_of_Labor" title="American Federation of Labor">American Federation of Labor</a> in May 1882,<sup id="cite_ref-Bridgemens1921_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bridgemens1921-21">[19]</a></sup> after witnessing the annual <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day#Canada_(country)" title="Labour Day">labour festival</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-origins_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-origins-22">[20]</a></sup> In 1887, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a> was the first state of the United States to make it an official <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">public holiday</a>. By the time it became an official <a href="/wiki/Federal_holiday" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal holiday">federal holiday</a> in 1894, thirty <a href="/wiki/US_state" class="mw-redirect" title="US state">US states</a> officially celebrated Labor Day.<sup id="cite_ref-Bridgemens1921_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bridgemens1921-21">[19]</a></sup> Thus by 1887 in North America, Labour Day was an established, official holiday but in September,<sup id="cite_ref-Knights_of_Labor_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knights_of_Labor-23">[21]</a></sup> not on 1 May. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg/220px-IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg/330px-IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg/440px-IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="982"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:IICCR_G005_May_1st_rally_in_Bucharest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A 1 May rally in <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a> in 1967
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>May Day has been a focal point for <a href="/wiki/Demonstration_(protest)" class="mw-redirect" title="Demonstration (protest)">demonstrations</a> by various socialist, communist and anarchist groups since the Second International. May Day is one of the most important holidays in communist countries such as <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and the former <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> countries. May Day celebrations in these countries typically feature elaborate workforce parades, including displays of military hardware and soldiers. </p>
      <p>In 1955, the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> dedicated 1 May to "<a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph" title="Saint Joseph">Saint Joseph</a> the Worker". Saint Joseph is the <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> of workers and craftsmen, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-Saint_Joseph_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saint_Joseph-24">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Today, the majority of countries around the world celebrate a workers' day on 1 May. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_Union_and_Eastern_Bloc_under_communist_governments">Soviet Union and Eastern Bloc under communist governments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Soviet Union and Eastern Bloc under communist governments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg/170px-RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg/255px-RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg/340px-RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="598" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_697507_May_1st_demonstration_in_Moscow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>May Day rally in Moscow, 1 May 1960
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> countries such as the Soviet Union and most countries of central and eastern Europe that were under the rule of <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxist-Leninist</a> governments held official May Day celebrations in every town and city, during which party leaders greeted the crowds. Workers carried banners with political slogans and many companies decorated their company cars. The biggest celebration of 1 May usually occurred in the capital of a particular communist country and usually included a military display and the presence of the president and the secretary general of the party. During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, May Day became the occasion for large <a href="/wiki/Military_parade" title="Military parade">military parades</a> in <a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">Red Square</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and attended by the top leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Kremlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Kremlin">Kremlin</a>, especially the <a href="/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Politburo of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Politburo</a>, atop <a href="/wiki/Lenin%27s_Mausoleum" title="Lenin's Mausoleum">Lenin's Mausoleum</a>. It became an enduring symbol of that period. In <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, since 1982, party leaders led the official parades. In Hungary, May Day was officially celebrated under the communist regime, and remains a public holiday. Traditionally, the day was marked by dancing around designated "May trees".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup> Some factories in communist countries were named in honour of International Workers' Day, such as <a href="/wiki/1_Maja_Coal_Mine" title="1 Maja Coal Mine">1 Maja Coal Mine</a> in <span lang="pl" style="font-style: normal;" title="Polish-language text">Wodzisław Śląski</span>, Poland. In <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>, the holiday was officially known as <i><i lang="de" title="German-language text">Internationaler Kampf- und Feiertag der Werktätigen für Frieden und Sozialismus</i></i> ("International Day of the Struggle and Celebration of the Workers for Peace and Socialism"); similar names were used in other Eastern Bloc countries. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="By_country">By country</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: By country">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day_RGBY.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day_RGBY.svg/310px-Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day_RGBY.svg.png" decoding="async" width="310" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day_RGBY.svg/465px-Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day_RGBY.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day_RGBY.svg/620px-Observance_of_International_Workers%27_Day_RGBY.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1406" data-file-height="592"></a>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Algeria">Algeria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Algeria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, 1 May is a public holiday celebrated as Labour Day.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Angola">Angola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Angola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is recognized as public holiday in <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> and called Workers' Day.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:DSC_1498_(5676929076).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/DSC_1498_%285676929076%29.jpg/220px-DSC_1498_%285676929076%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/DSC_1498_%285676929076%29.jpg/330px-DSC_1498_%285676929076%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/DSC_1498_%285676929076%29.jpg/440px-DSC_1498_%285676929076%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1339"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:DSC_1498_(5676929076).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Egyptian Communist Party flags in <a href="/wiki/Tahrir_Square" title="Tahrir Square">Tahrir Square</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, 1 May is known as Labour Day and is considered a paid holiday. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Egypt" title="President of Egypt">President of Egypt</a> traditionally presides over the official May Day celebrations.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Ethiopia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, 1 May is a public holiday and celebrated as Worker's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ghana">Ghana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ghana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is a holiday in <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>. It is a day to celebrate all workers across the country. It is celebrated with a parade by trade unions and labour associations.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-30">[28]</a></sup> The parades are normally addressed by the Secretary General of the trade union congress and by regional secretaries in the regions.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-30">[28]</a></sup> Workers from different workplaces through banners and T-shirts identify their companies.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-30">[28]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kenya">Kenya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Kenya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, 1 May is a public holiday and celebrated as Labour Day. It is a big day addressed by the leaders of the workers' umbrella union body – the <a href="/wiki/Central_Organization_of_Trade_Unions_(Kenya)" title="Central Organization of Trade Unions (Kenya)">Central Organisation of Trade Unions</a> (COTU). The Minister for Labour (and occasionally the President) address the workers. Each year, the government approves (and increases) the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a> on Labour Day.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Libya">Libya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Libya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, International Workers' Day was declared a national public holiday by the <a href="/wiki/National_Transitional_Council" title="National Transitional Council">National Transitional Council</a> in 2012 the first year of the post-Qaddafi era.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 1 May 1978, then <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libyan</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Muammar Gaddafi">Colonel Mu'ammar Al-Qaddafi</a> addressed the nation in the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a> calling for <a href="/wiki/Administration_(law)" title="Administration (law)">administrative</a> and also economic <a href="/wiki/History_of_Libya_under_Muammar_Gaddafi#Reforms_(1977–1980)" title="History of Libya under Muammar Gaddafi">reforms across Libya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Morocco">Morocco</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Morocco">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, 1 May is recognized as a public holiday on 1 May.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mozambique">Mozambique</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Mozambique">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Celebrates workers day on 1 May in <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Namibia">Namibia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Namibia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is recognized as public holiday in <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> and celebrated as Workers' Day.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nigeria">Nigeria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Nigeria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Since 1981, 1 May is a public holiday in <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>. On the day, people gather while, traditionally, the president of the <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_Labour_Congress" title="Nigeria Labour Congress">Nigeria Labour Congress</a> and other politicians address workers.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Somalia">Somalia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Somalia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, 1 May is a public holiday and celebrated as the Labour Day.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, Workers' Day has been celebrated as a national public holiday on 1 May each year since 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup> May Day started to get more attention by African workers in 1928, which saw thousands of workers in a mass march. In 1950, the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Communist_Party" title="South African Communist Party">South African Communist Party</a> called for a strike on 1 May in response to the <a href="/wiki/Suppression_of_Communism_Act,_1950" title="Suppression of Communism Act, 1950">Suppression of Communism Act</a> declaring it illegal. Police violence caused the death of 18 people across Soweto. It has its origins within the historical struggles of workers and their trade unions internationally for solidarity between working people in their struggles to win fair employment standards and more importantly, to establish a culture of human and worker rights and to ensure that these are enshrined in international law and the national law.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1986, the hundredth anniversary of the Haymarket affair, the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_South_African_Trade_Unions" title="Congress of South African Trade Unions">Congress of South African Trade Unions</a> (COSATU) called for the government to establish an official holiday on 1 May. It also called for workers to stay home from work that day.<sup id="cite_ref-SABC_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SABC-41">[39]</a></sup> COSATU was joined by a number of prominent anti-<a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> organizations, including the <a href="/wiki/Internal_resistance_to_apartheid#National_Education_Crisis_Committee" title="Internal resistance to apartheid">National Education Crisis Committee</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Democratic_Front_(South_Africa)" title="United Democratic Front (South Africa)">United Democratic Front (South Africa)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SAHO_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAHO-42">[40]</a></sup> The call was also supported by a number of organizations regarded as conservative, such as the African Teachers Association, the <a href="/wiki/National_African_Federated_Chamber_of_Commerce" title="National African Federated Chamber of Commerce">National African Federated Chamber of Commerce</a>, and the Steel and Engineering Industries Federation of South Africa, an organization that represented employers in the metal industries.<sup id="cite_ref-SAHO_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAHO-42">[40]</a></sup> More than 1,500,000 workers observed the call and stayed home, as did thousands of students, taxi drivers, vendors, shopkeepers, domestic workers, and self-employed people.<sup id="cite_ref-SAHO_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAHO-42">[40]</a></sup> In the following years, 1 May became a popular, if not official, holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-SABC_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SABC-41">[39]</a></sup> As a result of the killings on May Day 1950 and the success of COSATU's call in 1986, 1 May became associated with resistance to the apartheid government. After its <a href="/wiki/1994_South_African_general_election" title="1994 South African general election">first universal election in 1994</a>, 1 May was adopted as a public holiday, celebrated for the first time in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-SABC_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SABC-41">[39]</a></sup> On its website, the city of <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a> states that the holiday "celebrate[s] the role played by trade unions and other labour movements in the fight against South Africa's apartheid regime".<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tanzania">Tanzania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tanzania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>, it is a public holiday on 1 May and celebrated as the Worker's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tunisia">Tunisia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tunisia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1st_of_May_protest,_Tunis,_Tunisia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/1st_of_May_protest%2C_Tunis%2C_Tunisia.jpg/220px-1st_of_May_protest%2C_Tunis%2C_Tunisia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/1st_of_May_protest%2C_Tunis%2C_Tunisia.jpg/330px-1st_of_May_protest%2C_Tunis%2C_Tunisia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/1st_of_May_protest%2C_Tunis%2C_Tunisia.jpg/440px-1st_of_May_protest%2C_Tunis%2C_Tunisia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1st_of_May_protest,_Tunis,_Tunisia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>May Day rally in <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>1 May is recognized as Labour Day within <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Uganda">Uganda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Uganda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, Labour Day is a public holiday on 1 May.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Zimbabwe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is recognized as public holiday in <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> and called Workers' Day.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas">Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Argentina">Argentina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Argentina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, Workers' Day is an official holiday on 1 May, and is frequently associated with labour unions. Celebrations related to labour are held including demonstrations in major cities. </p>
      <p>The first Workers' Day celebration was in 1890, when Argentinian unions organized several celebrations in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a> and other cities, at the same time that the international labour movement celebrated it for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-ElHistoriador_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ElHistoriador-48">[46]</a></sup> In 1930, it was established as an official holiday by the <a href="/wiki/Radical_Civic_Union" title="Radical Civic Union">Radical Civic Union</a> president <a href="/wiki/Hip%C3%B3lito_Yrigoyen" title="Hipólito Yrigoyen">Hipólito Yrigoyen</a>. The day became particularly significant during the worker-oriented government of <a href="/wiki/Juan_Domingo_Per%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan Domingo Perón">Juan Domingo Perón</a> (1946–55).<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> He permitted and endorsed national recognition of the holiday during his tenure in office. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bolivia">Bolivia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Bolivia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is known as Labour Day and is a holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <b>Workers' Day</b> is an official holiday that is celebrated on 1 May, and unions commemorate it with day-long public events.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Canada, <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a> is celebrated in September. In 1894, the government of Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Sparrow_David_Thompson" title="John Sparrow David Thompson">John Sparrow David Thompson</a> declared the first Monday in September as Canada's official Labour Day. Labor Day in the United States is on the same day. </p>
      <p>May Day is however marked by unions and leftists. It is celebrated on 1 May. May Day is an important day of trade union and community group protest in the province of <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> (though not a provincial <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Canada" title="Public holidays in Canada">state holiday</a>). Celebration of the International Labour Day (or "International Workers' Day"; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Journée internationale des travailleurs</i>) in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a> goes back to 1906, organized by the Mutual Aid circle. The tradition had a renaissance at the time of a mass strike in 1972. On the 1973 May Day, the first contemporary demonstration was organized by the major trade union confederations; over 30,000 trade unionists took part in this demonstration. Further, it is the customary date on which the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage_in_Canada" title="Minimum wage in Canada">minimum wage</a> rises.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Protestas_Parque_O%60Higgins.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Protestas_Parque_O%60Higgins.jpg/300px-Protestas_Parque_O%60Higgins.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Protestas_Parque_O%60Higgins.jpg/450px-Protestas_Parque_O%60Higgins.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Protestas_Parque_O%60Higgins.jpg/600px-Protestas_Parque_O%60Higgins.jpg 2x" data-file-width="726" data-file-height="459"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Protestas_Parque_O%60Higgins.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Protest against the <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship_of_Chile_(1973%E2%80%931990)" title="Military dictatorship of Chile (1973–1990)">Pinochet dictatorship</a> in <a href="/wiki/O%27Higgins_Park" title="O'Higgins Park">O'Higgins Park</a>, Santiago, on 1 May 1984
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>President <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Ib%C3%A1%C3%B1ez_del_Campo" title="Carlos Ibáñez del Campo">Carlos Ibáñez del Campo</a> decreed 1 May a national holiday in 1931, in honour of the dignity of workers.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> All stores and public services must close for the entire day, and the major trade unions of Chile, represented in the national organization <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_United_Center_of_Chile" title="Workers' United Center of Chile">Workers' United Center of Chile</a> (Central Unitaria de Trabajadores), organize rallies during the morning hours, with festivities and cookouts in the later part of the day, in all the major cities of Chile. During these rallies, representatives of the major left-wing political parties speak to the assemblies on the issues of the day concerning workers' rights. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Colombia">Colombia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Colombia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May has long been recognized as Labour Day and almost all workers respect it as a national holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> As in many other countries, it is common to see rallies by the trade unions in all over the main regional capitals of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Costa_Rica">Costa Rica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Costa Rica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>First celebrated in 1913,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> labor day is a public holiday, and at the same time an important day for government activities. On this day, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Costa_Rica" title="President of Costa Rica">President of Costa Rica</a> gives a speech to the citizens and the <a href="/wiki/Legislature_of_Costa_Rica" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislature of Costa Rica">legislature of Costa Rica</a> about the duties that were undertaken through the previous year. The president of the legislature is also chosen by its members.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>This day is known as Labour Day in Cuba. People march in the streets, showing their support to the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Cuba" title="Communist Party of Cuba">Cuban Communist</a> government and the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> during the whole morning.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominican_Republic">Dominican Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Dominican Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is a national holiday known as Labour Day and celebrated by workers' parades and demonstration. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecuador">Ecuador</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Ecuador">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Ecuador, 1 May is an official public holiday known as Labour Day. People do not go to work and spend time with their relatives or gather for demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="El_Salvador">El Salvador</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: El Salvador">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is an official public holiday known as Labour Day.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Guatemala">Guatemala</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Guatemala">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is an official public holiday known as Labour Day.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Haiti">Haiti</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Haiti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is an official public holiday known as Agriculture and Labour Day.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Honduras">Honduras</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Honduras">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is an official holiday, known as "Labour Day" within Honduras.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is a federal holiday. It also commemorates the <a href="/wiki/Cananea_Strike" class="mw-redirect" title="Cananea Strike">Cananea Strike</a> of 1906 in the Mexican state of <a href="/wiki/Sonora" title="Sonora">Sonora</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Panama">Panama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Panama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is an official public holiday, known as "Labour Day" within Panama.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Paraguay">Paraguay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Paraguay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is an official public holiday, known as "Labour Day" within Paraguay.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Peru">Peru</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Peru">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is an official public holiday, known as "Labour Day" within Peru.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">Labor Day</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Socialists_in_Union_Square,_N.Y.C..jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Socialists_in_Union_Square%2C_N.Y.C..jpg/220px-Socialists_in_Union_Square%2C_N.Y.C..jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Socialists_in_Union_Square%2C_N.Y.C..jpg/330px-Socialists_in_Union_Square%2C_N.Y.C..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Socialists_in_Union_Square%2C_N.Y.C..jpg/440px-Socialists_in_Union_Square%2C_N.Y.C..jpg 2x" data-file-width="5779" data-file-height="4260"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Socialists_in_Union_Square,_N.Y.C..jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Socialists in Union Square, New York City, on 1 May 1912
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the United States, a "Labor Day", celebrated on the first Monday of each September was given increasing state recognition from 1887, and became an official <a href="/wiki/Federal_holiday" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal holiday">federal holiday</a> in 1894.<sup id="cite_ref-Knights_of_Labor_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knights_of_Labor-23">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Efforts to switch Labor Day from September to 1 May<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> have not been successful. </p>
      <p>In 1947, 1 May was established as <a href="/wiki/Loyalty_Day" title="Loyalty Day">Loyalty Day</a> by the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Veterans_of_Foreign_Wars" title="Veterans of Foreign Wars">Veterans of Foreign Wars</a> as a way to counter communist influence and recruitment at May Day rallies.<sup id="cite_ref-CredoLoyalty_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CredoLoyalty-67">[65]</a></sup> Loyalty Day was celebrated across the country with patriotic parades and ceremonies, however the growing conflict over U.S. involvement in Vietnam detracted from the popularity of these celebrations.<sup id="cite_ref-CredoLoyalty_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CredoLoyalty-67">[65]</a></sup> In 1958, the <a href="/wiki/American_Bar_Association" title="American Bar Association">American Bar Association</a> campaigned to have 1 May designated as <a href="/wiki/Law_Day_(United_States)" title="Law Day (United States)">Law Day</a>, which was acknowledged in 1961 by a joint resolution of Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> Law Day exercises, such as mock trials and courthouse tours, are often sponsored by the American Bar Association. </p>
      <p>Unions and <a href="/wiki/Political_radicalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Political radicalism">radical</a> organizations including <a href="/wiki/American_Left" title="American Left">anarchist groups and socialist and communist parties</a> have kept the international May Day tradition alive with rallies and demonstrations. In 1919 especially large demonstrations took place, and violence greeted the normally peaceful parades in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a> and <a href="/wiki/May_Day_Riots_of_1919" class="mw-redirect" title="May Day Riots of 1919">a number of people were killed</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> In Milwaukee, an annual commemoration takes place at the site of the killing of seven workers during an 8 hour march.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-15">[14]</a></sup> Some of the largest examples of this occurred during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> of the 1930s, when hundreds of thousands of workers marched in May Day <a href="/wiki/Parade" title="Parade">parades</a> in New York's <a href="/wiki/Union_Square_(New_York_City)" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Square (New York City)">Union Square</a>, while cities like <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duluth,_Minnesota" title="Duluth, Minnesota">Duluth</a> saw large demonstrations organized by the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_USA" title="Communist Party USA">communist party</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg/220px-San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg/330px-San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg/440px-San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2336"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:San_Jose_May_Day_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a>, May Day March, 1 May 2006
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2006, 1 May was chosen by mostly <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Latino</a> <a href="/wiki/Immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrant">immigrant</a> groups in the United States as the day for the <a href="/wiki/Great_American_Boycott" title="Great American Boycott">Great American Boycott</a>, a <a href="/wiki/General_strike" title="General strike">general strike</a> of undocumented immigrant workers and supporters to protest <a href="/wiki/Border_Protection,_Anti-terrorism,_and_Illegal_Immigration_Control_Act_of_2005" class="mw-redirect" title="Border Protection, Anti-terrorism, and Illegal Immigration Control Act of 2005">H.R. 4437</a>, immigration reform legislation that they felt was draconian. From 10 April to 1 May of that year, immigrant families in the U.S. called for immigrant rights, workers' rights and amnesty for undocumented workers. They were joined by socialist and other leftist organizations on 1 May.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> On 1 May 2007, a mostly peaceful demonstration in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> in support of undocumented immigrant workers ended with a widely televised <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_May_Day_m%C3%AAl%C3%A9e" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles May Day mêlée">dispersal by police officers</a>. In March 2008, the <a href="/wiki/International_Longshore_and_Warehouse_Union" title="International Longshore and Warehouse Union">International Longshore and Warehouse Union</a> announced that <a href="/wiki/Stevedore" title="Stevedore">dockworkers</a> will move no <a href="/wiki/Cargo" title="Cargo">cargo</a> at any <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">West Coast</a> ports on 1 May 2008, as a protest against the continuation of the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a> and the diversion of resources from domestic needs.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 1 May 2012, members of <a href="/wiki/Occupy_Wall_Street" title="Occupy Wall Street">Occupy Wall Street</a> and labor unions held protests together in a number of cities in the United States and Canada to commemorate May Day and to protest the state of the economy and economic inequality.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:International_Workers_Day_march_in_Minneapolis_(4570066628).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/International_Workers_Day_march_in_Minneapolis_%284570066628%29.jpg/220px-International_Workers_Day_march_in_Minneapolis_%284570066628%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/International_Workers_Day_march_in_Minneapolis_%284570066628%29.jpg/330px-International_Workers_Day_march_in_Minneapolis_%284570066628%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/International_Workers_Day_march_in_Minneapolis_%284570066628%29.jpg/440px-International_Workers_Day_march_in_Minneapolis_%284570066628%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:International_Workers_Day_march_in_Minneapolis_(4570066628).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Anarchists" class="mw-redirect" title="Anarchists">Anarchists</a> during may day, occupying streets
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 1 May 2017, immigrants' rights advocates, labor unions and leftists held protests against the immigration and economic policies of President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> in cities throughout the US, Chicago and Los Angeles having some of the largest marches.<sup id="cite_ref-wapo-1may2017_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wapo-1may2017-76">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytimes-1may2017_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-1may2017-77">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 1 May 2020, during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, "workers from at <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whole_Foods_Market" title="Whole Foods Market">Whole Foods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Instacart" title="Instacart">Instacart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a>, <a href="/wiki/FedEx" title="FedEx">FedEx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shipt" title="Shipt">Shipt</a> say they will walk off the job ... to protest their employers’ failure to provide basic protections for frontline workers who are risking and losing their lives at work."<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> Additionally, on the same day, there will be a <a href="/wiki/Rent_strike" title="Rent strike">rent strike</a>, the largest in nearly a century.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Uruguay">Uruguay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Uruguay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Uruguay, 1 May – Workers' Day – is an official holiday. Even when it is associated with labour unions, almost all workers tend to respect it. Since the late 1990s, the main event takes place at the <a href="/w/index.php?title=First_of_May_Square,_Montevideo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="First of May Square, Montevideo (page does not exist)">First of May Square</a> in Montevideo. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela">Venezuela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Venezuela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is an official holiday in Venezuela. <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">El Día del Trabajador</i> is celebrated on 1 May in Venezuela since 1936, but from 1938 to 1945 it was held on 24 July, by an order of <a href="/wiki/Eleazar_L%C3%B3pez_Contreras" title="Eleazar López Contreras">Eleazar López Contreras</a>. However, <a href="/wiki/Isa%C3%ADas_Medina_Angarita" title="Isaías Medina Angarita">Isaías Medina Angarita</a> changed it back to 1 May in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Asia">East Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: East Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainland_China">Mainland China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Mainland China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1952-05_1952%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%88%E4%BA%94%E4%B8%80%E5%8A%B3%E5%8A%A8%E8%8A%82.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/1952-05_1952%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%88%E4%BA%94%E4%B8%80%E5%8A%B3%E5%8A%A8%E8%8A%82.png/220px-1952-05_1952%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%88%E4%BA%94%E4%B8%80%E5%8A%B3%E5%8A%A8%E8%8A%82.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/1952-05_1952%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%88%E4%BA%94%E4%B8%80%E5%8A%B3%E5%8A%A8%E8%8A%82.png/330px-1952-05_1952%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%88%E4%BA%94%E4%B8%80%E5%8A%B3%E5%8A%A8%E8%8A%82.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/1952-05_1952%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%88%E4%BA%94%E4%B8%80%E5%8A%B3%E5%8A%A8%E8%8A%82.png/440px-1952-05_1952%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%88%E4%BA%94%E4%B8%80%E5%8A%B3%E5%8A%A8%E8%8A%82.png 2x" data-file-width="873" data-file-height="562"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1952-05_1952%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%88%E4%BA%94%E4%B8%80%E5%8A%B3%E5%8A%A8%E8%8A%82.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>International Workers' Day celebration in Beijing on 1 May 1952
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>1 May is a statutory holiday in the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a>. Prior to 2008, it was a three-day holiday, but is now just the one day.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> However, it is usually supplemented by two other days to give the appearance of a three-day holiday, but not being statutory holidays the extra days have to be "made up" by working either the preceding or following weekend.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> For example, in 2013, 1 May fell on Wednesday. Most workplaces, including all government offices, took Monday 29 April, Tuesday 30 April, and Wednesday 1 May off. As the first two days were not statutory holidays they had to be "made up" by working the preceding weekend (27 and 28 April). </p> 
      <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Hong_Kong">Hong Kong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Hong Kong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, 1 May is known as Labour Day and has been considered a public holiday since 1999. </p> 
      <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Macau">Macau</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Macau">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>, it is a public holiday and is officially known as <i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">Dia do Trabalhador</i> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> for "Workers' Day").<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan">Taiwan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Taiwan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is known as Labor Day in <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, an official holiday, though not everybody gets a day off. Students and teachers do not have this day off.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg/220px-NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg/330px-NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/35/NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="266"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:NUGW_May_Day_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>2011 <a href="/wiki/Zenrokyo" class="mw-redirect" title="Zenrokyo">National Trade Union Council (<i>Zenrokyo</i>)</a> May Day march, Tokyo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>May Day is not officially designated by the Japanese government as a national holiday, but as it lies between other national holidays, it is a day off work for the vast majority of Japanese workers. Many employers give it as a day off, and otherwise workers take it as "paid leave". 1 May occurs during "<a href="/wiki/Golden_Week_(Japan)" title="Golden Week (Japan)">Golden Week</a>", together with 29 April ("<a href="/wiki/Sh%C5%8Dwa_Day" title="Shōwa Day">Shōwa Day</a>"), 3 May ("<a href="/wiki/Constitution_Memorial_Day" title="Constitution Memorial Day">Constitution Memorial Day</a>"), 4 May ("<a href="/wiki/Greenery_Day" title="Greenery Day">Greenery Day</a>") and 5 May ("<a href="/wiki/Kodomo_no_hi" class="mw-redirect" title="Kodomo no hi">Children's Day</a>").<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> Workers generally take the day off work not so much to join street rallies or labour union gatherings, but more to go on holiday for several consecutive days (in Japanese corporate culture, taking weekdays off for personal pleasure is widely frowned upon). </p>
      <p>Some major labour unions organize rallies and demonstrations in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nagoya" title="Nagoya">Nagoya</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Japan has a long history of labour activism and has had a communist and socialist party in the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Diet" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Diet">Diet</a> since 1945. In 2008, the National Confederation of Trade Unions (<i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zenr%C5%8Dren&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Zenrōren (page does not exist)">Zenrōren</a></i>) held a rally in <a href="/wiki/Yoyogi_Park" title="Yoyogi Park">Yoyogi Park</a> attended by 44,000 participants, while the National Trade Unions Council (<i><a href="/wiki/Zenrokyo" class="mw-redirect" title="Zenrokyo">Zenrōkyō</a></i>) held its May Day rally at <a href="/wiki/Hibiya_Park" title="Hibiya Park">Hibiya Park</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <i><a href="/wiki/RENGO" title="RENGO">Rengō</a></i>, the largest Japanese trade union, held its May Day rally on the following Saturday (3 May), allegedly to distance itself from the more radical labour unions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Korea">North Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: North Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_People%27s_Republic_of_Korea" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic People's Republic of Korea">Democratic People's Republic of Korea</a>, 1 May is known as International Workers' Day, and is a public holiday. Celebrations, local meetings and rallies are held every year throughout the country to honor the holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Rungnado_May_Day_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Rungnado May Day Stadium">Rungnado May Day Stadium</a> in the capital of <a href="/wiki/Pyongyang" title="Pyongyang">Pyongyang</a> is named in honor of the holiday. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Korea">South Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: South Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Korea" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Korea">Republic of Korea</a>, 1 May is known simply as "Workers' Day". It is not a public holiday, but a paid holiday for workers by the <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/ko:%EB%8C%80%ED%95%9C%EB%AF%BC%EA%B5%AD_%EA%B7%BC%EB%A1%9C%EC%9E%90%EC%9D%98%EB%82%A0%EC%A0%9C%EC%A0%95%EC%97%90%EA%B4%80%ED%95%9C%EB%B2%95%EB%A5%A0" class="extiw" title="s:ko:대한민국 근로자의날제정에관한법률">Designation of Workers' Day Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[nb 3]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Albania">Albania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Albania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Labour Day (<a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>: <i lang="sq">Dita e punëtorëve</i>) is an official holiday celebrated on 1 May and thus schools and most businesses are closed.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Armenia">Armenia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Armenia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Labour Day (<a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>: <span lang="hy">Աշխատանքի օր</span>, <i lang="hy-Latn" title="Armenian-language text">ashxatanki or</i>) is an official holiday celebrated on 1 May.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[84]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Austria">Austria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Austria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Labour Day (<i lang="de" title="German-language text">Tag der Arbeit</i>), officially called <i lang="de" title="German-language text">Staatsfeiertag</i> (state's holiday), is a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Austria" title="Public holidays in Austria">public holiday in Austria</a>. Left parties, especially social democrats organize celebrations with marches and speeches in all major cities. In smaller towns and villages those marches are held the night before. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Belgium">Belgium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Belgium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Belgium, Labour Day (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Dag van de Arbeid</i>, <i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">Feest van de Arbeid</i>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Journée des travailleurs</i>, <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Fête du travail</i>), is observed on 1 May and is an <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Belgium" title="Public holidays in Belgium">official holiday</a> since 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[85]</a></sup> Various socialist and communist organizations hold parades and other events in different cities.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[86]</a></sup> </p>
