      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bosnia_and_Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Bosnia and Herzegovina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Bosnia and Herzegovina, 1 and 2 May (<a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">Bosnian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <i lang="sr-Latn">Prvi Maj</i> / <span lang="sr-Cyrl" title="Serbian-language text">Први Mај</span>, <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>: <i lang="hr">Prvi Svibanj</i>) are an official holiday and day-off for public bodies and schools at the national level. Most people celebrate this holiday by visiting natural parks and resorts. Additionally, in some places public events are organized. In its capital city, Sarajevo, 12 and 13 June are also celebrated as Labour day<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> due to its many natural parks and springs. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Bulgaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Labour Day is one of the <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Bulgaria" title="Public holidays in Bulgaria">public holidays in Bulgaria</a>, where it is known as <i>Labour Day and International Workers' Solidarity Day</i> (<a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>: <span lang="bg">Ден на труда и на международната работническа солидарност</span>) and celebrated annually on 1 May.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[87]</a></sup> The first attempt to celebrate it was in 1890 by the Bulgarian Typographical Association. In 1939, Labour Day was declared an official holiday. Since 1945 the communist authorities in the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Bulgaria" title="People's Republic of Bulgaria">People's Republic of Bulgaria</a> began to celebrate the holiday every year. After the end of socialism in Bulgaria in 1989 Labour Day continues to be an official and public holiday, but state authorities are not committed to the organization of mass events.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Croatia">Croatia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Croatia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Croatia, 1 May is a national holiday. Many public events are organized and held all over the country where bean soup is given out to all people as a symbol of a real workers' dish. Red carnations are also handed out to symbolise the origin of the day. In <a href="/wiki/Zagreb" title="Zagreb">Zagreb</a>, the capital, a major gathering is in <a href="/wiki/Maksimir_Park" title="Maksimir Park">Maksimir Park</a>, which is located in the east part of Zagreb. In Split, city on the coast, people go to Marjan, a park-forest at the western end of Split peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[88]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cyprus">Cyprus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Cyprus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Cyprus, 1 May (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">Εργατική Πρωτομαγιά</span>) is considered as an official Public Holiday (Labour Day). In general, all stores remain closed in public and private sector. The Labor Union and Syndicates celebrate with various festivals and events across the country. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Czech_Republic">Czech Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Czech Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In the Czech Republic, 1 May is an official and national holiday known as Labour Day (<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i lang="cs">Svátek práce</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Denmark">Denmark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Denmark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, 1 May is not an official holiday, but a variety of individuals, mostly in the public sector, construction industry, and production industry, get a half or a whole day off. It was first celebrated in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> in 1890. The location of the first celebration, the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A6lledparken" title="Fælledparken">Fælledparken</a>, still plays an important part today with speeches by politicians and trade unionists to mark the occasion. Many other events are also held around the country to commemorate the day.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Estonia">Estonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Estonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, 1 May is a public holiday and celebrated as part of May Day (Kevadpüha). It also coincides with Walpurgis Day (volbripäev). </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Finland">Finland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Finland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg/220px-Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg/330px-Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg/440px-Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg 2x" data-file-width="735" data-file-height="543"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vappu2005kuvaPK.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A May Day rally in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>, Finland
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In Finland, 1 May is an official and national holiday. Apart from Workers' Day (officially: <i lang="fi" title="Finnish-language text">suomalaisen työn päivä</i>, "day of Finnish labour"), it is also celebrated as a feast of students, and spring, called <i lang="fi" title="Finnish-language text"><a href="/wiki/Vappu" class="mw-redirect" title="Vappu">vappu</a></i> or Walpurgis Night.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[91]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Wpi_france.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Wpi_france.jpg/220px-Wpi_france.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Wpi_france.jpg/330px-Wpi_france.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Wpi_france.jpg/440px-Wpi_france.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wpi_france.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>May Day demonstration in <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a>, France
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In France, 1 May is a public holiday. It is, in fact, the only day of the year when employees are legally obliged to be given leave, save professions that cannot be interrupted due to their nature (such as workers in hospitals and public transport).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[92]</a></sup> Demonstrations and marches are a Labour Day tradition in France, where trade unions organize parades in major cities to defend workers' rights. It is also customary to offer a <a href="/wiki/Lily_of_the_valley" title="Lily of the valley">lily of the valley</a> to friends or family. This custom dates back to 1561, when king <a href="/wiki/Charles_IX_of_France" title="Charles IX of France">Charles IX</a>, aged 10, waiting for his accession to the throne, gave a lily of the valley to all ladies present. Today, the fiscal administration exempts individuals and workers' organizations from any tax or administrative duties related to the sales of lilies of the valley, provided they are gathered from the wild, and not bought to be resold. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In April 1933, the recently installed <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi government</a> declared 1 May the "Day of National Work", an official state holiday, and announced that all celebrations were to be organized by the government. Any separate celebrations by <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Germany" title="Communist Party of Germany">Communists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democrats</a> or <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">labour unions</a> were banned.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, 1 May remained a state holiday in both <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>. In communist <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>, workers were <i>de facto</i> required to participate in large state-organized parades on May Day.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Today in Germany it is simply called "Labour Day" (<i lang="de" title="German-language text">Tag der Arbeit</i>), and there are numerous demonstrations and celebrations by independent workers' organizations. Today, <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> witnesses yearly demonstrations on May Day, the largest organised by labour unions, political parties, the <a href="/wiki/Far_left" class="mw-redirect" title="Far left">far left</a> and the leftist <i lang="de" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Autonomism" title="Autonomism">Autonomen</a></i>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_(168).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_%28168%29.jpg/220px-1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_%28168%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_%28168%29.jpg/330px-1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_%28168%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_%28168%29.jpg/440px-1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_%28168%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1._Mai_2013_in_Hannover._Gute_Arbeit._Sichere_Rente._Soziales_Europa._Umzug_vom_Freizeitheim_Linden_zum_Klagesmarkt._Menschen_und_Aktivit%C3%A4ten_(168).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>May Day rally in <a href="/wiki/Hanover" title="Hanover">Hanover</a>, Germany, 1 May 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 1987, May Day has also become known for riots in some districts of Berlin. After police actions against radical leftists in that year's annual demonstrations, the <a href="/wiki/Autonomism" title="Autonomism">Autonomen</a> scattered and sought cover at the ongoing annual street fair in <a href="/wiki/Kreuzberg" title="Kreuzberg">Kreuzberg</a>. Three years prior to the <a href="/wiki/Reunification_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Reunification of Germany">reunification of Germany</a>, violent protests would only take place in the former <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a>. The protesters began tipping over police cars, violently resisting arrest, and began building <a href="/wiki/Barricade" title="Barricade">barricades</a> after the police withdrew due to the unforeseen resistance. Cars were set on fire, shops plundered and burned to the ground. The police eventually ended the riots the following night. These violent forms of protests by the radical left later increasingly involved participants without political motivation.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Annual street fairs have proven an effective way to prevent riots, and May Day in 2005 and 2006 have been among the most peaceful known to Berlin in nearly 25 years. In recent years, <a href="/wiki/Neo-Nazism" title="Neo-Nazism">neo-Nazis</a> and other groups on the <a href="/wiki/Far_right" class="mw-redirect" title="Far right">far right</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="National Democratic Party of Germany">National Democratic Party of Germany</a>, have used the day to schedule public demonstrations, often leading to clashes with left-wing protesters, which turned especially violent in <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a> in 1998 and 2005.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>May Day violence flared up again in 2010. After an approved far-right demonstration was blocked by leftists, a parade by an estimated 10,000 leftists and anarchists turned violent and resulted in an active response by the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Police" title="Berlin Police">Berlin Police</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Greece">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Greece 1 May is an optional public holiday. The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Labour_and_Social_Affairs_(Greece)" title="Ministry of Labour and Social Affairs (Greece)">Ministry of Labour</a> retains the right to classify it as an official public holiday on an annual basis, and it customarily does so.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[95]</a></sup> The day is called <i lang="el-Latn" title="Greek-language text">Ergatikí Proto-magiá</i> (<span lang="el" title="Greek-language text">Εργατική Πρωτομαγιά</span>, <abbr title="literally">lit.</abbr> "Workers' 1 May") and celebrations are marked by demonstrations in which left-wing political parties, anti-authority groups, and workers' unions participate. On May Day in 2010, there were major protests all over Greece, most notably <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, by many left, anarchist and communist supporters and some violent clashes with <a href="/wiki/Riot_police" title="Riot police">riot police</a> who were sent out to contain the protesters. They opposed economic reforms, an end to job losses and wage cuts in the face of the government's proposals of massive public spending cuts. These reforms are to fall in line with the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a>-<a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a>-<a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">ECB</a> loan proposals, which demand that Greece liberalize its economy and cut its public spending and private sector wages, which many believe will decrease living standards.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hungary">Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Hungary celebrates 1 May as a national holiday, with open-air festivities and fairs all over the country. Many towns raise May poles and festivals with various themes are organized around the holiday. Left-wing parties and trade unions hold public rallies commemorating Labour Day.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[97]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Iceland">Iceland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: Iceland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Iceland the Labour Day (<a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a>: <i lang="is">Baráttudagur verkalýðsins</i>) is a public holiday. The first demonstration for workers rights in Iceland occurred in 1923. A parade composed of trade unions and other groups marches through towns and cities across the country and speeches are delivered.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup> However, some private businesses are open, mainly in the capital.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Irish_Congress_of_Trade_Unions" title="Irish Congress of Trade Unions">Irish Congress of Trade Unions</a> (ITUC) marks May Day with rallies take place in <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> and other events such as lectures, concerts and film screenings also take place around a wider May Day festival.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[101]</a></sup> The first Monday in May has been a <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Public holiday in the Republic of Ireland">public holiday in the Republic of Ireland</a> since 1994<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[102]</a></sup> and in Northern Ireland since 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[103]</a></sup> In the Republic the public holiday was demanded by the ITUC<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[104]</a></sup> and proposed by the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Ireland)" title="Labour Party (Ireland)">Labour Party</a> in negotiating <a href="/wiki/23rd_Government_of_Ireland" title="23rd Government of Ireland">its 1992–94 coalition government</a> with <a href="/wiki/Fianna_F%C3%A1il" title="Fianna Fáil">Fianna Fáil</a>, and marked the centenary of the ITUC's predecessor, the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Trades_Union_Congress" title="Irish Trades Union Congress">Irish Trades Union Congress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[105]</a></sup> The public holiday has no official designation, as "Workers' Day" or otherwise.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[106]</a></sup> In 2005, Labour's <a href="/wiki/Ruairi_Quinn" title="Ruairi Quinn">Ruairi Quinn</a> condemned, as a slight to workers, an alleged Fianna Fáil proposal to replace the May holiday with one on 24 April commemorating the <a href="/wiki/1916_Rising" class="mw-redirect" title="1916 Rising">1916 Rising</a>; in fact the proposal was for an extra holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg/220px-Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg/330px-Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg/440px-Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rome_concert_1-5-2007_crowd_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Traditional 1st May Concert in St. John Lateran square, <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The first May Day celebration in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> took place in 1890. It started initially as an attempt to celebrate workers' achievements in their struggle for their rights and for better social and economic conditions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It was abolished under the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_under_Fascism_(1922%E2%80%931943)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Italy under Fascism (1922–1943)">Fascist regime</a> and immediately restored after the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. (During the fascist period, a "Holiday of the Italian Labour" (<i lang="it" title="Italian-language text">Festa del lavoro italiano</i>) was celebrated on 21 April, the date of <i lang="it" title="Italian-language text">Natale di Roma</i>, when ancient <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> was allegedly founded.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>) May Day is now an important celebration in Italy and is a national holiday regardless of what day of the week it falls. The <i lang="it" title="Italian-language text">Concerto del Primo Maggio</i> ("1st of May Concert"), organized by Italian labour unions in Rome in <a href="/wiki/Porta_San_Giovanni_(Rome)" title="Porta San Giovanni (Rome)">Piazza di Porta San Giovanni</a> has become an important event in recent years. Every year the concert is attended by a large audience of mostly young people and involves the participation of many famous bands and songwriters, lasting from 3&nbsp;pm until midnight. The concert is usually broadcast live by <a href="/wiki/Rai_3" title="Rai 3">Rai 3</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lithuania">Lithuania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Lithuania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>First May Day is an official public holiday celebrated as International Work Day (<a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a>: <i lang="lt">Tarptautinė darbo diena</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[108]</a></sup> Celebrations for workers' day were mandatory during the <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states" title="Occupation of the Baltic states">Soviet occupation</a>, and carry a negative connotation as a result today. As Lithuania <a href="/wiki/Act_of_the_Re-Establishment_of_the_State_of_Lithuania" title="Act of the Re-Establishment of the State of Lithuania">declared its independence</a> in 1990, Work Day lost its public holiday status, but regained it in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Latvia">Latvia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: Latvia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>First May Day is an official public holiday celebrated as Convocation of the Constituent Assembly of the Republic of Latvia, Labour Day.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[111]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: Luxembourg">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Luxembourg, 1 May, called the <i lang="lb" title="Luxembourgish-language text">Dag vun der Aarbecht</i> ("Day of Labour"), is a legal holiday traditionally associated with large demonstrations by trade unions in Luxembourg City and other cities.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Malta">Malta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Malta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Malta, 1 May is an official public holiday celebrated as "Workers' Day",<sup id="cite_ref-maltagov_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maltagov-116">[113]</a></sup> together with the <a href="/wiki/Religious_feast" class="mw-redirect" title="Religious feast">religious feast</a> of "<a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph" title="Saint Joseph">Saint Joseph</a> the Worker". (<a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_Day" title="Saint Joseph's Day">Saint Joseph's Day</a>, 19 March, the saint's main feast, is also a public holiday in Malta.<sup id="cite_ref-maltagov_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maltagov-116">[113]</a></sup>) A free music event takes place on 1 May. The Maltese also celebrate <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">Maltese accession to the European Union</a> on 1 May 2004. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Montenegro">Montenegro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Montenegro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is an official public holiday and a day off work and a day out of school. It is the only official holiday from socialist times that is still officially celebrated.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[114]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In the Netherlands, 1 May or Labour Day (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Dag van de Arbeid</i>) is not an official holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[115]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Macedonia">North Macedonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=79" title="Edit section: North Macedonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Prvomajska_proslava_vo_Skopje,_1909.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Prvomajska_proslava_vo_Skopje%2C_1909.jpg/220px-Prvomajska_proslava_vo_Skopje%2C_1909.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Prvomajska_proslava_vo_Skopje%2C_1909.jpg/330px-Prvomajska_proslava_vo_Skopje%2C_1909.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Prvomajska_proslava_vo_Skopje%2C_1909.jpg/440px-Prvomajska_proslava_vo_Skopje%2C_1909.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1383" data-file-height="925"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Prvomajska_proslava_vo_Skopje,_1909.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>First <a href="/wiki/May_Day" title="May Day">May Day</a> celebration of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman period</a> in <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a>, 1909
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In North Macedonia, 1 May (<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">Ден на Трудот</span>, <i lang="mk-Latn" title="Macedonian-language text">Den na Trydot</i>) is an official public holiday. Before 2007, 2 may was also a public holiday. People celebrate with friends and family at traditional picnics across the country, accompanied by the usual outdoor games, various grilled meats and beverages. Left organizations and some trade unions organize protests on 1 May.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[116]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Norway">Norway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=80" title="Edit section: Norway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg/220px-Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg/330px-Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg/440px-Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="333"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jens_stoltenberg1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Norway's former Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jens_Stoltenberg" title="Jens Stoltenberg">Jens Stoltenberg</a> gives his 1 May speech in 2009 in <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, Norway.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In Norway, Labour Day (<a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a>: <i lang="no">Arbeidernes Dag</i>) is celebrated 1 May and is an official public holiday. It is traditionally a day of marches, speeches and parties organized by <a href="/wiki/Labour_union" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour union">labour unions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leftist" class="mw-redirect" title="Leftist">leftist</a> <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political parties</a> and <a href="/wiki/Feminist" class="mw-redirect" title="Feminist">feminist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anti-racist" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-racist">anti-racist</a> organizations to voice political concerns and celebrate <a href="/wiki/Solidarity" title="Solidarity">solidarity</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=81" title="Edit section: Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG/220px-Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG/330px-Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG/440px-Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wodzis%C5%82aw_KWK_1_Maja.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/1_Maja_Coal_Mine" title="1 Maja Coal Mine">1st May Coal Mine</a> in Wodzisław Śląski, Poland
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In Poland, since the fall of communism, 1 May is officially celebrated as <a href="/wiki/May_Day" title="May Day">May Day</a>, but is commonly called <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Poland" title="Public holidays in Poland">Labour Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[118]</a></sup> it is currently celebrated without a specific connotation, and as such it is May Day. However, due to historical connotations, most of the large organized celebrations are focused around Labour Day festivities. It is customary for labour activists to organize parades in cities and towns across Poland. The holiday is also commonly referred to as "Labour Day" (<a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <i lang="pl">Święto Pracy</i>). </p>
      <p>In Poland, May Day is closely followed by <a href="/wiki/May_3rd_Constitution_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="May 3rd Constitution Day">May 3rd Constitution Day</a>. These two dates combined often result in a <a href="/wiki/Long_weekend" title="Long weekend">long weekend</a> called <i lang="pl" title="Polish-language text">Majówka</i>, which may last for up to 9 days from 28 April to 6 May, at the cost of taking only 3 days off. People often travel, and <i lang="pl" title="Polish-language text">Majówka</i> is unofficially considered the start of barbecuing season in Poland.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Between these two, on 2 May, there is a patriotic holiday, the Day of the Polish Flag (<i lang="pl" title="Polish-language text"><a href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dzie%C5%84_Flagi_Rzeczypospolitej_Polskiej" class="extiw" title="pl:Dzień Flagi Rzeczypospolitej Polskiej">Dzień Flagi Rzeczypospolitej Polskiej</a></i>), introduced by a Parliamentary Act of 20 February 2004. The day, however, does not force paid time off. </p>
      <p>In Soviet times, streets, places, squares, parks and also factories were frequently named in honor of International Workers' Day, such as <a href="/wiki/1_Maja_Coal_Mine" title="1 Maja Coal Mine">1 Maja Coal Mine</a> in <span lang="pl" style="font-style: normal;" title="Polish-language text"><a href="/wiki/Wodzis%C5%82aw_%C5%9Al%C4%85ski" title="Wodzisław Śląski">Wodzisław Śląski</a></span>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Portugal">Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=82" title="Edit section: Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Portugal, the 1 May celebration (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">Primeiro de Maio</i>) was suppressed during the dictatorship of <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Oliveira_Salazar" title="António de Oliveira Salazar">António de Oliveira Salazar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Caetano" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcelo Caetano">Marcelo Caetanos</a> <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo</a> regime. The first workers' day demonstration was held a week after the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> of 25 April 1974. It is still the largest demonstration in the history of Portugal. It is used as an opportunity for workers and workers' groups to voice their discontent over working conditions in demonstrations across Portugal, the largest being held in Lisbon. It is an official public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[119]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=83" title="Edit section: Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:002_State_and_party_leaders_celebrating_May_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/002_State_and_party_leaders_celebrating_May_1.jpg/220px-002_State_and_party_leaders_celebrating_May_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/002_State_and_party_leaders_celebrating_May_1.jpg/330px-002_State_and_party_leaders_celebrating_May_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/002_State_and_party_leaders_celebrating_May_1.jpg/440px-002_State_and_party_leaders_celebrating_May_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1073" data-file-height="1002"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:002_State_and_party_leaders_celebrating_May_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Delegates of the Romanian Communist Party on 1 May 1965
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In Romania, 1 May, known as the <b>International Labour Day</b> (<a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>: <i lang="ro">Ziua internațională a muncii</i>), the <b>International Workers' Day</b> (<i lang="ro" title="Romanian-language text">Ziua internațională a oamenilor muncii</i>), or simply <b>1/First of May</b> (<i lang="ro" title="Romanian-language text">1/Întâi Mai</i>), is an official <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Romania" title="Public holidays in Romania">public holiday</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Romania" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Romania">communist regime</a>, like in all former Eastern Bloc countries, the day was marked by large state-organized parades in most towns and cities. After the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Revolution_of_1989" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian Revolution of 1989">Romanian Revolution of 1989</a>, 1 May continues to be an official public holiday, but without any state organized events or parades. Most people celebrate together with friends and family, organising <a href="/wiki/Picnic" title="Picnic">picnics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbecue" title="Barbecue">barbecues</a>. It is also the first day of the year when people, especially those from the southeastern part of the country including the capital <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>, go to spend the day in one of the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Black_Sea_resorts" title="Romanian Black Sea resorts">Romanian Black Sea resorts</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=84" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage"
