        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kuban_Cossacks_1937.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kuban_Cossacks_1937.jpg/220px-Kuban_Cossacks_1937.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kuban_Cossacks_1937.jpg/330px-Kuban_Cossacks_1937.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kuban_Cossacks_1937.jpg/440px-Kuban_Cossacks_1937.jpg 2x" data-file-width="842" data-file-height="550"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kuban_Cossacks_1937.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mounted <a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">cossacks</a> during an International Workers' Day <a href="/wiki/Military_parade" title="Military parade">military parade</a> in 1937
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>May Day, also known in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> as the <b>Day of International Workers Solidarity, the 1st of May</b> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">День международной солидарности трудящихся Первое ма́я</span>) was celebrated illegally in the country until the <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution" title="February Revolution">February Revolution</a> enabled the first legal celebration in 1917. The following year, after the <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik">Bolshevik</a> <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">seizure of power</a>, the May Day celebrations were boycotted by <a href="/wiki/Mensheviks" title="Mensheviks">Mensheviks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Left_Socialist_Revolutionaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Left Socialist Revolutionaries">Left Socialist Revolutionaries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_in_Russia" title="Anarchism in Russia">anarchists</a>. It became an important official holiday of the Soviet Union, celebrated with elaborate popular parade in the centre of the major cities. The biggest celebration was traditionally organized in <a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">Red Square</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_CPSU" class="mw-redirect" title="General Secretary of the CPSU">General Secretary of the CPSU</a> and other party and government leaders stood atop <a href="/wiki/Lenin%27s_Mausoleum" title="Lenin's Mausoleum">Lenin's Mausoleum</a> and waved to the crowds. Until 1969, the holiday was marked by <a href="/wiki/Military_parade" title="Military parade">military parades</a> throughout the <a href="/wiki/RSFSR" class="mw-redirect" title="RSFSR">RSFSR</a> and the union republics.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[120]</a></sup> The following was the order of the march past: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Parade commander holding the appointment of commanding officer of the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Military_District" title="Moscow Military District">Moscow Military District</a></li> 
       <li>Corps of Drums of the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Military_Music_College" title="Moscow Military Music College">Moscow Military Music College</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Frunze_Military_Academy" title="Frunze Military Academy">Frunze Military Academy</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Lenin_Military-Political_Academy" title="Lenin Military-Political Academy">V.I. Lenin Military Political Academy</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Felix_Dzerzhinsky_Artillery_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Felix Dzerzhinsky Artillery Academy">Felix Dzerzhinsky Artillery Academy</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Malinovsky_Military_Armored_Forces_Academy" title="Malinovsky Military Armored Forces Academy">Military Armored Forces Academy Marshal Rodion Malinovsky</a></li> 
       <li>Military Engineering Academy</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/NBC_Protection_Military_Academy" title="NBC Protection Military Academy">Military Academy of Chemical Defense and Control</a></li> 
       <li>Yuri <a href="/wiki/Gagarin_Air_Force_Academy" title="Gagarin Air Force Academy">Gagarin Air Force Academy</a></li> 
       <li>Prof. Nikolai <a href="/wiki/Zhukovsky_Air_Force_Engineering_Academy" title="Zhukovsky Air Force Engineering Academy">Zhukovsky Air Force Engineering Academy</a></li> 
       <li>Delegation of naval officer cadets from the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Navy" title="Soviet Navy">Soviet Navy</a><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[121]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/98th_Guards_Airborne_Division" title="98th Guards Airborne Division">98th Guards Airborne Division</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Moscow_Border_Institute_of_the_FSB_of_the_Russian_Federation" title="Moscow Border Institute of the FSB of the Russian Federation">Moscow Border Guards Institute of the Border Defence Forces of the KGB "Moscow City Council"</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Separate_Operational_Purpose_Division" title="Separate Operational Purpose Division">Separate Operational Purpose Division</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/336th_Guards_Naval_Infantry_Brigade" title="336th Guards Naval Infantry Brigade">336th Marine Brigade</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Fleet" title="Baltic Fleet">Baltic Fleet</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Suvorov_Military_School" title="Suvorov Military School">Suvorov Military School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nakhimov_Naval_School" title="Nakhimov Naval School">Nakhimov Naval Schools</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Moscow_Higher_Military_Command_School" title="Moscow Higher Military Command School">Moscow Military Combined Arms Command Training School "Supreme Soviet of the Russian SFSR"</a></li> 
       <li>Mobile Column 
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/2nd_Guards_Motor_Rifle_Division" title="2nd Guards Motor Rifle Division">2nd Guards Motor Rifle Division</a></li> 
         <li>4th Guards Tank Division</li> 
         <li>Missile Troops and Artillery of the Moscow Military District</li> 
         <li>1st Aerospace Defense Army</li> 
         <li><a href="/wiki/Northern_Fleet" title="Northern Fleet">Northern Fleet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Fleet" title="Baltic Fleet">Baltic Fleet</a> Coastal Defense, Surface and Submarine Forces (until 1974)</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Military_Band_Service_of_the_Armed_Forces_of_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Military Band Service of the Armed Forces of the Soviet Union">Massed Bands of the Moscow Military District</a> (parade finale)</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The first of these parades were held <a href="/wiki/1918_May_1_Parade" title="1918 May 1 Parade">1918</a>, when <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> presided over a ceremony at <a href="/wiki/Khodynka_Field" title="Khodynka Field">Khodynka Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[122]</a></sup> Notable parades included the parade of 1941 (which saw the presence of a <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a> delegation led by <a href="/wiki/Ernst_August_K%C3%B6string" title="Ernst August Köstring">Ernst August Köstring</a><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[123]</a></sup>) and 1963 (where Cuban leader <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> was a guest). The only parades on 1 May to be cancelled were the parades scheduled during the years of the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> and the 1965 parade (this was cancelled to make way for the <a href="/wiki/1965_Moscow_Victory_Day_Parade" title="1965 Moscow Victory Day Parade">1965 Moscow Victory Day Parade</a> nine days later). In 1979, ten years after the last annual parade, a brief <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_drill" title="Exhibition drill">exhibition drill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_tattoo" title="Military tattoo">military tattoo</a> of the forces of the Moscow Garrison took place.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[124]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1991, which preceded the last year that demonstrations were held in Red Square, May Day grew into high-spirited political action. Around 50,000 people participated in a rally in Red Square in 1991 after which the tradition was interrupted for 13 years. In the early post-Soviet period the holiday turned into massive political gatherings of supporters of radically minded politicians. For instance, an action dubbed as "a rally of communist-oriented organisations" was held in Red Square in 1992. The rally began with performance of the Soviet Union anthem and raising the Red Flag and ended with appeals from the leader of opposition movement Working Moscow, <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Anpilov" title="Viktor Anpilov">Viktor Anpilov</a>, "for early dismissal of President <a href="/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin" title="Boris Yeltsin">Boris Yeltsin</a>, ousting <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Mayor" class="mw-redirect" title="Moscow Mayor">Moscow Mayor</a> <a href="/wiki/Gavriil_Kharitonovich_Popov" class="mw-redirect" title="Gavriil Kharitonovich Popov">Gavriil Popov</a> from power and putting the latter on trial". Since 1992, May Day is officially called "The Day of Spring and Labour", and remains a major holiday in present-day Russia. </p>
      <p>Since 2014 a national civil parade is held on that day on Red Square with similar events held in major cities and regional capitals. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Serbia">Serbia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=85" title="Edit section: Serbia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Serbia, 1 May (and also 2 May) is a day off work and a day out of school. It is one of the major popular holidays, and the only official holiday from socialist times that is still officially celebrated. People celebrate it all over the country. By tradition 1 May is celebrated by countryside picnics and outdoor barbecues. May is marked by warm weather in Serbia. In <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, the capital, most people go to <span lang="sr" style="font-style: normal;" title="Serbian-language text"><a href="/wiki/Avala" title="Avala">Avala</a></span> or <span lang="sr" style="font-style: normal;" title="Serbian-language text"><a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1utnjak" title="Košutnjak">Košutnjak</a></span>, which are parks located in <span lang="sr" style="font-style: normal;" title="Serbian-language text">Rakovica</span> and <span lang="sr" style="font-style: normal;" title="Serbian-language text">Čukarica</span>. People go around the country to enjoy nature. A major religious holiday of <span lang="sr" style="font-style: normal;" title="Serbian-language text"><a href="/wiki/Djurdjevdan" class="mw-redirect" title="Djurdjevdan">Djurdjevdan</a></span> is on 6 May so quite often days off work are given to connect these two holidays and weekend, creating a small spring break. 1 May is celebrated by most of the population regardless of political views. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovakia">Slovakia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=86" title="Edit section: Slovakia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Slovakia, 1 May is an official holiday. Celebrations are held surrounding workers' day but are also connected with the commemoration of the <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">entry of the Slovak Republic into the European Union</a> (1 May 2004).<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[125]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovenia">Slovenia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=87" title="Edit section: Slovenia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Slovenia, 1 May and 2 May are public holidays. There are many official events all over the country to celebrate workers' day. In <a href="/wiki/Ljubljana" title="Ljubljana">Ljubljana</a>, the capital, the main celebration is held on <a href="/wiki/Ro%C5%BEnik_(hill)" title="Rožnik (hill)">Rožnik Hill</a> in the city. On the night of 30 April, bonfires are traditionally burned.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[126]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=88" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day_in_Spain" title="Labor Day in Spain">Labor Day in Spain</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG/220px-Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG/330px-Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG/440px-Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Manifestacio_barcelona_primer_de_maig_alternatiu_2009.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>May Day rally in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, Spain
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The first Día del Trabajador was celebrated in 1889 but only became a public holiday with the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Second_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Second Republic">Spanish Second Republic</a> in 1931. It was banned afterwards by the <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">Franco regime</a> in 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[127]</a></sup> The year after it was decreed that the "Fiesta de la Exaltacion del Trabajo," or Labor Festival, be held on 18 July, the anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_faction_(Spanish_Civil_War)" title="Nationalist faction (Spanish Civil War)">Francoist</a> <a href="/wiki/Spanish_coup_of_July_1936" title="Spanish coup of July 1936">military coup</a>, instead.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[128]</a></sup> After the death of <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> in 1975 and the move towards democracy, the first large rallies on 1 May began again in 1977. It was re-introduced as a public holiday in 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[129]</a></sup> Commonly, peaceful demonstrations and parades occur in major and minor cities.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[131]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=89" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg/220px-1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg/330px-1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg/440px-1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1236" data-file-height="918"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1maj2006soc.dem.sthlm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Swedish_Social_Democratic_Party" title="Swedish Social Democratic Party">Swedish Social Democratic Party</a> at May Day demonstration in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, in 2006. The party has dominated Swedish politics for nearly a century. The <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Trade_Union_Confederation" title="Swedish Trade Union Confederation">trade union palace</a> in Stockholm is seen at the end of the picture.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>1 May has been an important part of Swedish history since the late 19th century. The day was made a <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">public holiday</a> in 1938 but had been celebrated by the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Social_Democratic_Party" title="Swedish Social Democratic Party">Swedish Social Democratic Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4nsterpartiet" class="mw-redirect" title="Vänsterpartiet">left</a> since 1890. The first May Day celebration gathered more than 50,000 people in central Stockholm. The crowd went to hear speeches by the leading figures in the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_labour_movement" title="Swedish labour movement">Swedish labour movement</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Hjalmar_Branting" title="Hjalmar Branting">Hjalmar Branting</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a>), <a href="/wiki/August_Palm" title="August Palm">August Palm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hinke_Bergegren" title="Hinke Bergegren">Hinke Bergegren</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> the demonstrations mainly had a peace message and the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_People%27s_Party_(Sweden)" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberal People's Party (Sweden)">Liberal Party</a> also joined the demonstrations. The <a href="/wiki/8-hour_working_day" class="mw-redirect" title="8-hour working day">eight-hour working day</a> and <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage" title="Women's suffrage">women's suffrage</a> were the principal themes during the troubled times after World War I. </p>
      <p>Recognizing the central contributions of workers and international worker solidarity in Swedish social, economic, political and cultural development, May Day demonstrations are an important part of Swedish politics and culture for social democrats, left parties, and unions. In Stockholm the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Social_Democratic_Party" title="Swedish Social Democratic Party">Social Democratic Party</a> always marches towards <a href="/wiki/Norra_Bantorget" title="Norra Bantorget">Norra Bantorget</a>, the historical, physical centre of the Swedish labour movement, where they hold speeches in front of the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Trade_Union_Confederation" title="Swedish Trade Union Confederation">Swedish Trade Union Confederation</a>, while the smaller <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4nsterpartiet" class="mw-redirect" title="Vänsterpartiet">Left Party</a> marches in larger numbers<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[132]</a></sup> towards <a href="/wiki/Kungstr%C3%A4dg%C3%A5rden" title="Kungsträdgården">Kungsträdgården</a>. </p>
      <p>Since 1967, the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_(Sweden)" title="Communist Party (Sweden)">Communist Party</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Youth_wing" title="Youth wing">youth wing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Communist_Youth_(Sweden)" title="Revolutionary Communist Youth (Sweden)">Revolutionary Communist Youth</a>, have held their own May Day march, known as <i lang="sv" title="Swedish-language text">Röd Front</i> ('Red Front').<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[133]</a></sup> In 2016, Röd Front marches were held at 33 locations across the country.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[134]</a></sup> The largest Röd Front marches are usually held in the industrial and financial port town of <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg" title="Gothenburg">Gothenburg</a>, Sweden's second-largest city and one of the party's strongholds.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Parade_of_the_May_1_demonstrations_(70-ies)._(6984904464).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Parade_of_the_May_1_demonstrations_%2870-ies%29._%286984904464%29.jpg/220px-Parade_of_the_May_1_demonstrations_%2870-ies%29._%286984904464%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Parade_of_the_May_1_demonstrations_%2870-ies%29._%286984904464%29.jpg/330px-Parade_of_the_May_1_demonstrations_%2870-ies%29._%286984904464%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Parade_of_the_May_1_demonstrations_%2870-ies%29._%286984904464%29.jpg/440px-Parade_of_the_May_1_demonstrations_%2870-ies%29._%286984904464%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Parade_of_the_May_1_demonstrations_(70-ies)._(6984904464).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>May Day in the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> in the 1970s
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Switzerland">Switzerland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=90" title="Edit section: Switzerland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Switzerland, the status of 1 May differs depending on the <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Switzerland" title="Cantons of Switzerland">canton</a> and sometimes on the municipality. Labour Day is known as <i lang="de" title="German-language text">Tag der Arbeit</i> in German-speaking cantons, as <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Fête du travail</i> in the French-speaking cantons, and as <i lang="it" title="Italian-language text">Festa del lavoro</i> in the Italian-speaking canton of <span lang="it" style="font-style: normal;" title="Italian-language text"><a href="/wiki/Ticino" title="Ticino">Ticino</a></span>. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>In the cantons of <span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Basel-Landschaft" title="Basel-Landschaft">Basel-Landschaft</a></span>, <span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Basel-Stadt" title="Basel-Stadt">Basel-Stadt</a></span>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Jura" title="Canton of Jura">Jura</a>, <span lang="fr" style="font-style: normal;" title="French-language text"><a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Neuch%C3%A2tel" title="Canton of Neuchâtel">Neuchâtel</a></span>, and <span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Zurich" class="mw-redirect" title="Canton of Zurich">Zürich</a></span>, Labour Day is an official public holiday equal to Sundays, based on federal law (<i lang="de" title="German-language text">Bundesgesetz über die Arbeit in Industrie, Gewerbe und Handel</i>, article 20a).</li> 
       <li>In the cantons of <span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Schaffhausen" title="Canton of Schaffhausen">Schaffhausen</a></span>, <span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Thurgau" title="Thurgau">Thurgau</a></span>, and <span lang="it" style="font-style: normal;" title="Italian-language text">Ticino</span>, Labour Day is an official "day off" (<i lang="de" title="German-language text">Ruhetag</i>). This is equal in practice to an official public holiday, but is not based on federal law and cantonal regulations may differ in details.</li> 
       <li>In the canton of <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Solothurn" title="Canton of Solothurn">Solothurn</a> it is an official half-day holiday (starting at 12 noon).</li> 
       <li>In the canton of <span lang="fr" style="font-style: normal;" title="French-language text"><a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Fribourg" title="Canton of Fribourg">Fribourg</a></span>, public servants get the afternoon off, many companies follow this practice.</li> 
       <li>In the canton of <span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Aargau" title="Aargau">Aargau</a></span> it is not an official holiday, but most employees get the afternoon off.</li> 
       <li>In the municipalities of <span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Hildisrieden" title="Hildisrieden">Hildisrieden</a></span> and <span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%BCpfheim" title="Schüpfheim">Schüpfheim</a></span> (both in the canton of <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Lucerne" title="Canton of Lucerne">Lucerne</a>) as well as in <span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Muotathal" title="Muotathal">Muotathal</a></span> (canton of <span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Schwyz" title="Canton of Schwyz">Schwyz</a></span>), 1 May is an official public holiday, but as commemoration day of the local <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a>, not as Labour Day. In the other parts of the cantons of Lucerne and <span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;" title="German-language text">Schwyz</span>, 1 May is a regular work day.</li> 
       <li>In all other cantons, 1 May is a regular work day.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[137]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The largest Labour Day celebrations in Switzerland are held in the city of <span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a></span>. Each year, <span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;" title="German-language text">Zürich</span>'s 1 May committee, together with the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federation_of_Trade_Unions" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Federation of Trade Unions">Swiss Federation of Trade Unions</a>, organizes a festival and 1 May rally. It is the largest rally held on a regular basis in Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[138]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=91" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg/220px-May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg/330px-May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg/440px-May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:May_day_clashes_in_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Istanbul May Day clashes in 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG/220px-Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG/330px-Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG/440px-Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3174" data-file-height="1919"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_May_Day_2012.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Workers marching to <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Square" title="Taksim Square">Taksim Square</a>, 1 May 2012
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>1 May is an official holiday celebrated in Turkey. It was a holiday until 1981 when it was cancelled after the <a href="/wiki/1980_Turkish_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1980 Turkish coup d'état">1980 coup d'état</a>. In 2010, the Turkish government restored the holiday after some casualties and demonstrations. <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Square" title="Taksim Square">Taksim Square</a> is the centre of the celebrations due to the <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Square_massacre" title="Taksim Square massacre">Taksim Square massacre</a>. </p>
      <p>Workers' Day was first celebrated in 1912 in <span lang="tr" style="font-style: normal;" title="Turkish-language text"><a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stanbul" class="mw-redirect" title="İstanbul">İstanbul</a></span> and in 1899 in <span lang="tr" style="font-style: normal;" title="Turkish-language text"><a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmir" title="İzmir">İzmir</a></span>. After the establishment of the Turkish Republic, it became an official holiday. In 1924, it was forbidden by a decree and in both 1924 and 1925, demonstrations were intervened by arm floats. In 1935, The National Assembly declared Workers' Day to be a holiday again.<sup id="cite_ref-marksist.com_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksist.com-142">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the events leading to the 1980 Turkish coup d'etat, a massacre occurred on 1 May 1977 (Taksim Square massacre), in which unknown people (<a href="/wiki/Agent_provocateur" title="Agent provocateur">agents provocateurs</a>) opened fire on the crowd. The crowd was the biggest in Turkish workers' history with the number of people approximating 500,000. In the next two years, provocations and confusion continued and peaked before the 1980 coup d'etat. The Workers' Day holiday was cancelled once again. Still, demonstrations continued with small crowds, and in 1996, three people were killed by police bullets, and a plain-clothes man who spied in the crowd was revealed and lynched by workers. On the same evening, a video broadcast on TV showed that two participants in the demonstration were lynched by far right-wing nationalist groups and this lynching occurred in front of police forces who were watching the scene with happy faces. Thus, 1 May 1996 has been remembered by workers' movements.<sup id="cite_ref-marksist.com_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marksist.com-142">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2007, the 30th anniversary of the Taksim square massacre, leftist workers' unions wanted to commemorate the massacre in <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Square" title="Taksim Square">Taksim Square</a>. Since the government would not let them into the square, 580–700 people were stopped and 1 person died under police control. After these events, the government declared 1 May as "Work and Solidarity Day" but not as a holiday. In the next year, the day was declared as a holiday, but people were still not allowed to gather in Taksim Square.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[140]</a></sup> The year 2008 was remembered with police violence in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>. Police fired tear gas grenades among the crowds, and into hospitals and a primary school. Workers pushed forward so that in 2010, 140,000 people gathered in Taksim, and in 2011 there were more than half a million demonstrators. </p>
      <p>After three years of peaceful meetings in 2013, meetings in Taksim Square were forbidden by the government. Clashes occurred between police and workers; <a href="/wiki/Water_cannon" title="Water cannon">water cannon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tear_gas" title="Tear gas">tear gas</a> have been widely used.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[141]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukraine">Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=92" title="Edit section: Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>It is a public holiday in Ukraine, inherited from the Soviet era. May Day as a day of workers' solidarity in Kiev began as early as 1894.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[142]</a></sup> Until 2018, 2 May was also a public holiday (as in the Soviet era), instead in 2017 <a href="/wiki/Western_Christianity" title="Western Christianity">Western Christianity</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> celebrated 25 December became a new Ukrainian public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCU42008437b_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCU42008437b-147">[144]</a></sup> The 1 May International Workers' Day remained a Ukrainian public holiday, although it was renamed (also in 2017) from "Day of International Solidarity of Workers" to "Labour Day".<sup id="cite_ref-BBCU42008437b_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCU42008437b-147">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2015, May Day rallies were banned in <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv" title="Kharkiv">Kharkiv</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[145]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Late May 2015 <a href="/wiki/Decommunization_in_Ukraine" title="Decommunization in Ukraine">laws that ban communist symbols</a> came into effect in Ukraine, thus banning communist symbols, singing the Soviet national hymn or the Internationale.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[146]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to Interior Minister <a href="/wiki/Arsen_Avakov" title="Arsen Avakov">Arsen Avakov</a> during the 2016 May Day rallies in some major cities the number of <a href="/wiki/National_Police_of_Ukraine" title="National Police of Ukraine">police officers</a> far outnumbered the number of rally participants.<sup id="cite_ref-mptrmd16U_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mptrmd16U-150">[147]</a></sup> With in <a href="/wiki/Dnipro" title="Dnipro">Dnipro</a> 193 policemen protecting 25 rally participants.<sup id="cite_ref-mptrmd16U_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mptrmd16U-150">[147]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=93" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:May_Day_in_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/May_Day_in_London.jpg/220px-May_Day_in_London.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/May_Day_in_London.jpg/330px-May_Day_in_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/May_Day_in_London.jpg/440px-May_Day_in_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:May_Day_in_London.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Stalin banner belonging to the <a href="/wiki/CPGB-ML" class="mw-redirect" title="CPGB-ML">CPGB-ML</a>, featured in every London International Workers' Day rally since 2008
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A public bank holiday in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> known as May Day was created in 1978 and is held on the first Monday in May each year.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[148]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are many traditional <a href="/wiki/May_Day#United_Kingdom" title="May Day">May Day</a> rites and celebrations, some of which have been held for hundreds of years. However, it was not until the late 20th century that May Day in Great Britain became linked to International Workers' Day, and the holiday is not officially a "Labour Day". </p>
      <p>In recent years, the <a href="/wiki/Anti-capitalism" title="Anti-capitalism">anti-capitalist</a> movement has organized a number of large protests in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Doncaster" title="Doncaster">Doncaster</a>. In London, these have resulted in clashes with the police. In 2000, the clashes ended with a branch of <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> being smashed and a statue of <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> being given a grass <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_hairstyle" title="Mohawk hairstyle">Mohawk hairstyle</a>. The <a href="/wiki/The_Cenotaph,_Whitehall" class="mw-redirect" title="The Cenotaph, Whitehall">Cenotaph</a> was also defaced with <a href="/wiki/Graffiti" title="Graffiti">graffiti</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[150]</a></sup> In the last few years, demonstrations have been more peaceful, with marches and gatherings, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">central London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[151]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition" title="Cameron–Clegg coalition">Conservative-led coalition government</a> in March 2011 announced plans to move the May Day bank holiday to October to lengthen the tourist season,<sup id="cite_ref-MayDayabolishedUK_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MayDayabolishedUK-155">[152]</a></sup> although as of 2017 nothing had come of this. A London rally on May Day is organized by the London May Day Organising Committee. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=94" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=95" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Labourday1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Labourday1.jpg/220px-Labourday1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Labourday1.jpg/330px-Labourday1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Labourday1.jpg/440px-Labourday1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="488"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Labourday1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Labour Day March in <a href="/wiki/Brisbane,_Queensland" class="mw-redirect" title="Brisbane, Queensland">Brisbane, Queensland</a>, is the largest rally in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>While unofficial activities and commemorations associated with International Workers Day occur on May Day in Australia, <a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a> in the various states and territories generally falls on other days. Only in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">Northern Territory</a> (where it is called May Day) and <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a> is Labour Day celebrated on the first Monday in May, which is a public holiday under the name of "May Day". <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a> holds the biggest rallies in Australia, with the rally in <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a> averaging 30,000 people.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In Australia, one of the first May Day marches occurred in Queensland on 1 May 1891.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[153]</a></sup> There are also rallies held in <a href="/wiki/Cairns" title="Cairns">Cairns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rockhampton" title="Rockhampton">Rockhampton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Townsville" title="Townsville">Townsville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcaldine,_Queensland" title="Barcaldine, Queensland">Barcaldine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ipswich,_Queensland" title="Ipswich, Queensland">Ipswich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toowoomba" title="Toowoomba">Toowoomba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bundaberg" title="Bundaberg">Bundaberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryborough,_Queensland" title="Maryborough, Queensland">Maryborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunshine_Coast,_Queensland" title="Sunshine Coast, Queensland">Sunshine Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast,_Queensland" title="Gold Coast, Queensland">Gold Coast</a> and other regional centres.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=96" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> workers were among the first in the world to claim the right for an eight-hour working day when, in 1840, the carpenter <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Duncan_Parnell" title="Samuel Duncan Parnell">Samuel Parnell</a><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[154]</a></sup> won an eight-hour day in <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a>. Labour Day was first celebrated in New Zealand on 28 October 1890.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[155]</a></sup> Labour day falls every year on the fourth Monday of October. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Asia">South Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=97" title="Edit section: South Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=98" title="Edit section: Bangladesh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Bangladesh, 1 May Day is a public holiday and called May Day. A parade and other events are held on the day to commemorate the occasion.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[156]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=99" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg/220px-Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg/330px-Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg/440px-Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Triumph_of_Labour_at_Marina_Beach.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Triumph_of_Labour" title="Triumph of Labour">Triumph of Labour</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Marina_Beach" title="Marina Beach">Marina Beach</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In India, Labour Day is a public holiday held on every 1 May.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[157]</a></sup> The holiday is tied to labour movements for communist and socialist political parties. Labour Day is known as "Uzhaipalar dhinam" in <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a> and was first celebrated in <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Madras</a>, "Kamgar Din" in <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>, "Karmikara Dinacharane" in <a href="/wiki/Kannada" title="Kannada">Kannada</a>,"Karmika Dinotsavam" in <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a>, "Kamgar Divas" in <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a>, "Thozhilaali Dinam" in <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">Malayalam</a> and "Shromik Dibosh" in <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a>. Since Labour day is not a national holiday, Labour day is observed as public holiday at <a href="/wiki/State_governments_of_India" title="State governments of India">State Government</a>'s discretion. Many parts especially in <a href="/wiki/North_India" title="North India">North Indian States</a> it is not a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first celebration in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> was organized in Madras (now <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>) by the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Kisan_Party_of_Hindustan" title="Labour Kisan Party of Hindustan">Labour Kisan Party of Hindustan</a> on 1 May 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[159]</a></sup> This was also the first time the <a href="/wiki/Red_flag_(politics)" title="Red flag (politics)">red flag</a> was used in India.<sup id="cite_ref-rao1_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rao1-163">[160]</a></sup> The party leader <a href="/wiki/Malayapuram_Singaravelu_Chettiar" class="mw-redirect" title="Malayapuram Singaravelu Chettiar">Singaravelu Chettiar</a> made arrangements to celebrate May Day in two places in 1923. One meeting was held at the beach opposite to the <a href="/wiki/Madras_High_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="Madras High Court">Madras High Court</a>; the other meeting was held at the <a href="/wiki/Triplicane" title="Triplicane">Triplicane</a> beach. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hindu" title="The Hindu">The Hindu</a></i> newspaper, published from Madras reported,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[161]</a></sup> </p> 
      <blockquote>
       <p>The Labour Kisan party has introduced May Day celebrations in Madras. Comrade Singaravelar presided over the meeting. A resolution was passed stating that the government should declare May Day as a holiday. The president of the party explained the non-violent principles of the party. There was a request for financial aid. It was emphasised that workers of the world must unite to achieve independence.</p>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>1 May is also celebrated as "<a href="/wiki/Maharashtra_Day" title="Maharashtra Day">Maharashtra Day</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[162]</a></sup> and "<a href="/wiki/Gujarat_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Gujarat Day">Gujarat Day</a>" to mark the date in 1960, when the two western states attained statehood after the erstwhile <a href="/wiki/Bombay_State" title="Bombay State">Bombay State</a> was divided on linguistic lines. Maharashtra Day is held at <a href="/wiki/Shivaji" title="Shivaji">Shivaji</a> Park in central <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>. Schools and offices in Maharashtra remain closed on 1 May. A similar parade is held to celebrate <a href="/wiki/Gujarat_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Gujarat Day">Gujarat Day</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gandhinagar" title="Gandhinagar">Gandhinagar</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Vaiko" title="Vaiko">Vaiko</a> (Vai Gopalsamy), General Secretary of <a href="/wiki/Marumalarchi_Dravida_Munnetra_Kazhagam" title="Marumalarchi Dravida Munnetra Kazhagam">Marumalarchi Dravida Munnetra Kazhagam</a>, appealed to the then Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/V._P._Singh" class="mw-redirect" title="V. P. Singh">V. P. Singh</a> to declare 1 May as a national holiday, to which the PM heeded and from then on it became a national holiday to celebrate International Labour Day.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[163]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (June 2017)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Maldives">Maldives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=100" title="Edit section: Maldives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a> first observed the holiday in 2011, after a declaration by <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Maldives" title="President of the Maldives">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Nasheed" title="Mohamed Nasheed">Mohamed Nasheed</a>. He noted that this move highlighted the government's commitment as well as efforts of private parties to protect and promote workers' rights in the Maldives.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[164]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nepal">Nepal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=101" title="Edit section: Nepal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May Day has been celebrated in <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> since 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[165]</a></sup> The day became a public holiday in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[166]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=102" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>International Labour Day is observed in Pakistan on 1 May to commemorate the social and economic achievements of workers. It is a public and national holiday. Many organized street demonstrations take place on Labor Day, where workers and labor unions protest against labor repression and demand for more rights, better wages and benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[167]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sri_Lanka">Sri Lanka</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=103" title="Edit section: Sri Lanka">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Sri Lanka, it is observed on 1 May and is a government and public holiday. The government has held official May Day celebrations in major towns and cities, with the largest being in the capital, <a href="/wiki/Colombo" title="Colombo">Colombo</a>. During celebrations, it is common to witness party leaders greeting the crowds. Workers frequently carry banners with political slogans and many parties decorate their vehicles. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Asia">Southeast Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=104" title="Edit section: Southeast Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cambodia">Cambodia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=105" title="Edit section: Cambodia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Cambodia, it is known as International Labour Day and is a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[168]</a></sup> No marches for labour day were permitted in Cambodia for several years after the <a href="/wiki/2013_Cambodian_general_election" title="2013 Cambodian general election">2013 Cambodian general election</a> and surrounding mass protetsts. A tightly controlled march on a limited scale was first permitted again in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[169]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">Indonesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=106" title="Edit section: Indonesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Protest_march_in_Jakarta,_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Protest_march_in_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg/220px-Protest_march_in_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Protest_march_in_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg/330px-Protest_march_in_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Protest_march_in_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg/440px-Protest_march_in_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg 2x" data-file-width="614" data-file-height="461"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Protest_march_in_Jakarta,_Indonesia_-_20070501.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Protest march in Jakarta, Indonesia, 1 May 2007
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>May Day (often referred locally as Labour Day) in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> was first observed as a public holiday from 2014. Every year on the day, labourers take over the streets in major cities across the country, voicing their demands for better income &amp; a supportive policy by the ministries.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[170]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=107" title="Edit section: Malaysia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> began observing the holiday in 1972 following an announcement by the late <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister_of_Malaysia" title="Deputy Prime Minister of Malaysia">Malaysian Deputy Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Abdul_Rahman" title="Ismail Abdul Rahman">Ismail Abdul Rahman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[171]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Myanmar">Myanmar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=108" title="Edit section: Myanmar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Myanmar, 1 May is known as Labour Day (<a href="/wiki/Burmese_language" title="Burmese language">Burmese</a>: <span lang="my">အလုပ်သမားနေ့</span>) and is a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[172]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=109" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is known as <b>Labor Day</b> (<a href="/wiki/Filipino_language" title="Filipino language">Filipino</a>: <i lang="fil">Araw ng mga Manggaggawa</i>) and is a <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday_in_the_Philippines" class="mw-redirect" title="Public holiday in the Philippines">public holiday in the Philippines</a>. On this day, labour organizations and unions hold protests in major cities. On 1 May 1903, during the <a href="/wiki/American_Colonial_Period_of_the_Philippines" class="mw-redirect" title="American Colonial Period of the Philippines">American colonial period</a> the <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text"><a href="/wiki/Uni%C3%B3n_Obrera_Democr%C3%A1tica_Filipina" title="Unión Obrera Democrática Filipina">Unión Obrera Democrática Filipina</a></i> (Filipino Democratic Labor Union) held a 100,000-person<sup id="cite_ref-InquirerLaborDay_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InquirerLaborDay-176">[173]</a></sup> rally in front of the <a href="/wiki/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace" title="Malacañang Palace">Malacañang Palace</a> demanding workers' economic rights and Philippine independence.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Ten years later, the first official<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (December 2013)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> celebration was held on 1 May 1913 when 36 labour unions convened for a congress in <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-InquirerLaborDay_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InquirerLaborDay-176">[173]</a></sup> On 1 May 2001, a mass demonstration occurred near <a href="/wiki/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace" title="Malacañang Palace">Malacañang Palace</a> known as <a href="/wiki/EDSA_3#May_1" class="mw-redirect" title="EDSA 3">EDSA 3</a> or 1 May Riots. </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo" class="mw-redirect" title="Presidency of Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo">Presidency of Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo</a>, a policy was adopted called <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_the_Philippines#&quot;Holiday_Economics&quot;" title="Public holidays in the Philippines">holiday economics</a> policy that moved holidays to either a Monday or a Friday to create a <a href="/wiki/Long_weekend" title="Long weekend">long weekend</a> of three days. In 2002, Labor Day was moved to the Monday nearest to 1 May. Labour groups protested, as they accused the Arroyo administration of belittling the holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[174]</a></sup> By 2008, Labor Day was excluded in the holiday economics policy, returning the commemorations to 1 May, no matter what day of the week it falls on.<sup id="cite_ref-GMGApr2008_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMGApr2008-1">[1]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Singapore">Singapore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=110" title="Edit section: Singapore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Singapore, it is known as Labour Day and is a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[175]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Thailand">Thailand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=111" title="Edit section: Thailand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Thailand, the day is known in English as National Labour Day, and is one of 17 official <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Thailand" title="Public holidays in Thailand">public holidays in Thailand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[176]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam">Vietnam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=112" title="Edit section: Vietnam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Vietnam, it is known as International Labour Day (<a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a>: <i lang="vi">Ngày Quốc tế Lao động</i>) and is a public holiday. It was first celebrated in 1913.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_Asia">West Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=113" title="Edit section: West Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bahrain">Bahrain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=114" title="Edit section: Bahrain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Bahrain, 1 May is known as Labour Day and is a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[177]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=115" title="Edit section: Iran">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, 1 May is known as the International Workers' Day. It is not a public holiday but according to article 63 of <a href="/wiki/Iranian_labour_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Iranian labour law">Iranian labour law</a> on top of the official public holidays observed in the Islamic Republic of Iran, Labour Day shall be considered an official holiday for workers.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[178]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Iraq">Iraq</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=116" title="Edit section: Iraq">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, it is known as the International Workers' Day and is a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[179]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=117" title="Edit section: Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG/220px-PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG/330px-PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG/440px-PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="525"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_2571_May_First_demonstration_%D7%94%D7%A4%D7%92%D7%A0%D7%AA_%D7%90%D7%97%D7%93_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%99.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Israel, 1 May 2007
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After historically varying popularity of Labour Day, 1 May is not an official holiday in the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Israel" class="mw-redirect" title="State of Israel">State of Israel</a>. In the 1980s there were several large marches in Tel Aviv, numbering as much as 350.000 in 1983 and perhaps even more in 1988, but a steady decline in numbers led to only 5000 marchers in 2010. During the 1990s businesses began to treat it like a regular working day as the number of May Day-related activities decreased.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[180]</a></sup> 1 May is largely celebrated by the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="History of the Jews in the Soviet Union">former Soviet Jews</a> who <a href="/wiki/1990s_post-Soviet_aliyah" title="1990s post-Soviet aliyah">immigrated to Israel</a> in the 1990s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Jordan">Jordan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=118" title="Edit section: Jordan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is known as Labour Day and is a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[181]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lebanon">Lebanon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=119" title="Edit section: Lebanon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May known as the Workers' Day and is a public holiday. Left-wing parties and workers' unions organize marches on 1 May.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[182]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Palestine">Palestine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=120" title="Edit section: Palestine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is known as Labour Day and is a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[185]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Syria">Syria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=121" title="Edit section: Syria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>1 May is known as Labour Day and is a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[186]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=122" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Workers%27_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=123" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style>
      <div class="reflist"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">I saw a man, whom I afterwards identified as Fielding [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>], standing on a truck wagon at the corner of what is known as Crane's Alley. I raised my baton and, in a loud voice, ordered them to disperse as peaceable citizens. I also called upon three persons in the crowd to assist in dispersing the mob. Fielding got down from the wagon, saying at the time, "We are peaceable," as he uttered the last word, I heard a terrible explosion behind where I was standing, followed almost instantly by an irregular volley of pistol shots in our front and from the sidewalk on the east side of the street, which was immediately followed by regular and well directed volleys from the police and which was kept up for several minutes. I then ordered the injured men brought to the stations and sent for surgeons to attend to their injuries. After receiving the necessary attention most of the injured officers were removed to the County Hospital and I highly appreciate the manner in which they were received by Warden McGarrigle who did all in his power to make them comfortable as possible.<sup id="cite_ref-William_Ward,_Capt._3rd_Prect_report_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-William_Ward,_Capt._3rd_Prect_report-13">[13]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"In 1884 the first Monday in September was selected as the holiday, as originally proposed"<sup id="cite_ref-labordept_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-labordept-19">[18]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-85"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-85">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>5월 1일을 근로자의 날로 하고 이 날을 "근로기준법"에 의한 유급휴일로 한다.</i> ("The first day of May each year shall be designated as Workers' Day, which shall be a paid holiday under the '<a href="/wiki/Labor_Standards_Act_(South_Korea)" title="Labor Standards Act (South Korea)">Labor Standards Act</a>'.)"<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup></span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>
